<script>
	function goToTopic(topic) {
		var topicMap = applySpecialCharacterMapping(topic); 
		var url = "/xpl/topicbrowse.jsp?topic=" + escape(topicMap);
		window.top.location.href = url;
	}
</script>

The inductively coupled feed structure is beneficial for conjugate impedance matching. The loaded capacitors in the radiating and feeding loops allow for easy control of the resonant frequency and the antenna reactance, respectively. The omnidirectional radiation pattern on the horizontal plane makes the proposed tag insensitive to be mounted on different target objects. With a small size of 43 × 43 mm<sup>2</sup>, the measured maximum reading range of the prototype is 9.5 m with a total transmitted power of 4.0 W effective isotropic radiated power (EIRP).</div>

<div id="BodyWrapper" class="ArticlePage" xmlns:ieee="http://www.ieeexplore.ieee.org"><div id="article">
<div class="section" id="sec1"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION I.</div><h2>Introduction</h2></div><p>Radio frequency identification (RFID) technology is a remote automatic identification technology, which enables target recognition and relevant data acquisition through radio frequency signals. In an RFID system, the tag antenna is a vital part, and its performance greatly affects the reading range and accuracy of the RFID system.</p><p>RFID technology has found many applications in the catering business, including food production in the kitchen, tracking of customers' tastes at the restaurant, and self-help settlement on the counter <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">[1]</a>. The dipole-type antenna, whose main radiation direction is perpendicular to the surface of the tag, has been adopted for most tags applied in the catering business <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">[1]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a>. However, there are still some cases in which dipole-type antennas are not practical. It is difficult to put a tag antenna on some vertical surfaces of the target object if the vertical surface is curved (like a bowl) or has little space (e.g., a plate). In these cases, tags have to be attached on horizontal surfaces of target objects, tags (represented by red colors) with dipole-type antennas can hardly be detected by a reader on the same horizontal plane. In such a case, an RFID antenna with an isotropic radiation pattern or a horizontally omnidirectional radiation pattern would be feasible, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1</a>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig1"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6478802/6590019/6590019-fig-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6478802/6590019/6590019-fig-1-small.gif" alt="Figure 1" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 1. </b><fig><p>Side view of radiation patterns of different tags.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6590019/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>Some RFID tag antennas with quasi-isotropic radiation patterns have been proposed in previous literature. The antenna in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a> comprises an open-loop radiating element and a small feeding loop. The maximum reading range of the implemented RFID tag is 2.6 m, with a total transmitted power of 0.5 W (effective isotropic radiated power, i.e., EIRP). In <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a>, an RFID tag antenna (which is a bent dipole in shape) for sushi plates tracking is proposed. The size is 60×60 mm<sup>2</sup>, and the reading range is 10–14 cm with an output power of 14 dBm and a reader antenna gain of 2 dBi. The antenna proposed in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a> consists of a bent dipole with a T-matching network and a ground plane with two slots. The simulated gain of the antenna is −3.6 dBi, and its size is 68×65 mm<sup>2</sup>. However, a tag antenna with a horizontally omnidirectional radiation pattern would have a higher gain in the horizontal plane than a tag antenna with an isotropic radiation pattern if these two tags have similar sizes. Furthermore, a tag antenna with a horizontally omnidirectional radiation pattern can be more reliable (less sensitive) than an antenna with an isotropic radiation pattern when attached on plates of different materials.</p><p>In order to achieve a horizontally omnidirectional radiation pattern, a capacitively loaded, inductively fed loop antenna is proposed in this letter. This antenna consists of a capacitively loaded radiating loop and a concentric inductively coupled feeding loop. With a size of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-1-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1" role="math" style="width: 7.631em; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-20"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-21"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-22" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">0</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-2">\lambda_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the corresponding wavelength of the operating frequency), the antenna achieves a maximum gain of −0.3 dB in the horizontal plane (while the value is −3.6 dB in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a>) and a maximum measured reading range of 9.5 m with a total transmitted power of 4.0 W EIRP. This maximum reading range is much longer than 7.4 m in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a> and 1.4 m in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a>, with the same total transmitted power.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec2"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION II.</div><h2>Antenna Configuration and Physical Mechanism</h2></div><p>The geometry of the proposed antenna is depicted in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2</a>. The antenna consists of outer and inner loops, which are the radiator and the feed, respectively. The two loops are made of 0.01 mm aluminum and printed on a polyethylene terephthalate (PET) substrate with a thickness of 0.05 mm and relative permittivity of 3.2. It is noted that the loops and substrate are represented by orange and gray colors in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2</a>, respectively. Four periodically spaced interdigital capacitors are inserted into the radiating loop to provide a very small phase correction between the adjacent sections so that the current flowing along the loop is kept in phase and uniform even though the perimeter of the loop is no longer electrically small <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_2">[6]</a>–<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_2">[7]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_2">[8]</a>. The inductively coupled feeding loop is applied in the proposed antenna for conjugate impedance matching to the application-specific integrated circuit (ASIC) chip <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_2">[9]</a>–<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_2">[10]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_2">[11]</a>. The interdigital capacitor inserted in the feeding loop makes the impedance matching even more convenient. The RFID chip is placed in the intersection of the feeding loop and the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-3-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-23" role="math" style="width: 0.664em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.604em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.54em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-24"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-25" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">x</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.67em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-3">x</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-axis. The details of the interdigital capacitors are shown in the inset. <div class="section" id="sec3"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION III.</div><h2>Equivalent Circuit and Parametric Studies</h2></div><p>To help better understand the working mechanism of the proposed loop antenna, an equivalent circuit is given and plotted in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3</a>. A modified equivalent circuit is obtained by making an analogy (with some differences as there is no loaded capacitor in the feeding loop and stray capacitances in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_3">[11]</a>) to those of the electrically small, capacitively loaded, inductively coupled fed loop antennas in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_3">[11]</a>. The radiating loop can be modeled as a series <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-14-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-108" role="math" style="width: 1.625em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.444em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.44em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-109"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-110" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-111" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">C<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-14">LC</script></tex-math></inline-formula> resonant circuit (the inductance and capacitance are presented by <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-15-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-112" role="math" style="width: 1.324em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.204em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.2em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-113"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-114"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.204em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-115" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-15">L_{\rm rl}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-16-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-120" role="math" style="width: 1.444em; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.784em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-132"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-133"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-134" style="font-size: 70.7%; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.724em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-140"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-141"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-142" style="font-size: 70.7%; The loading of four periodically spaced interdigital capacitors allows the current flowing along the loop to keep in phase even when the perimeter of the loop is <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-19-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-144" role="math" style="width: 3.126em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.826em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1002.83em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-145"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-146" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">0.38</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-147"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-148" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">λ</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-149"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-150"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-151" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">0</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-19">0.38\lambda_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. In addition, it introduces a series capacitance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-20-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-152" role="math" style="width: 1.444em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.264em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.26em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-153"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-154"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.264em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-155" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">C<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.724em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-156"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-157"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-158" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">r</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-159" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">l</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-20">C_{\rm rl}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, which contributes to the self-resonance of the radiating loop.</p><p>

font-family: MathJax_Main;">p</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-167" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">r</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; It depends on the size of the radiating loop. The equivalent circuit of the feeding loop is similar to that of the radiating loop. The series inductance, capacitance, and resistance are represented by <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-22-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-168" role="math" style="width: 1.324em; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-22">L_{\rm fl}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-23-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-176" role="math" style="width: 1.444em; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.841em; left: 0.784em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-188"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-189"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-190" style="font-size: 70.7%; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-195" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">C<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.841em; left: 0.724em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-196"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-197"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-198" style="font-size: 70.7%; vertical-align: -0.397em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-25">C_{\rm pf}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The inductive coupling between the radiating and feeding loops can be represented by a transformer, which plays a critical role in impedance matching. The mutual inductance is denoted by <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-26-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-200" role="math" style="width: 1.144em; The extracted equivalent circuit parameters are listed in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table1" class="fulltext-link">Table I</a>. The detailed process of parameter extraction can be found in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_3">[11]</a>. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 4</a> shows the results of input resistance <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-36-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-350" role="math" style="width: 2.465em; It is seen that the two methods agree well with each other, only with tiny frequency deviation, which is due to separated simulations of the radiating and feeding loops during the extraction of their parameters.</p><p>Next, some key parameters are analyzed, from which the working mechanism of such a design is further illustrated and a rough design procedure can also be summarized. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 5(a)</a> shows the shift of the resonant frequency of the antenna when the length <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-38-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-370" role="math" style="width: 1.144em; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-67">\Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> [as in <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn1" href="#deqn1" class="fulltext-link">(1)</a>].</p></li></ol><p></p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec4"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION IV.</div><h2>Experimental Results and Discussions</h2></div><p>The proposed tag antenna is designed in a roll-to-roll (R2R) process. A Monza 4 chip with an input impedance of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-68-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-578" role="math" style="width: 5.348em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.808em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.75em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-579"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-580" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">11</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-581" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">−</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-582" style="padding-left: 0.243em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-583"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-584" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">j</span></span></span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-585" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">143</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-586" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Ω</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-68">11-{\rm j}143 \Omega</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and a threshold power sensitivity of −17.4 dBm at 915 MHz is used in the experiment.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig6"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6478802/6590019/6590019-fig-6-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6478802/6590019/6590019-fig-6-small.gif" alt="Figure 6" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 6. </b><fig><p>Photograph of fabricated antenna prototype.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6590019/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig7"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6478802/6590019/6590019-fig-7-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6478802/6590019/6590019-fig-7-small.gif" alt="Figure 7" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 7. </b><fig><p>(a) Measured and simulated input impedance. (b) Measured and simulated power reflection coefficients.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6590019/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>A prototype of the proposed antenna (as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 6</a>) was fabricated and measured with Agilent E8358A. The desired operating frequency of this antenna is 915 MHz, and at this frequency the size of the radiating loop is only <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-69-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-587" role="math" style="width: 7.631em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 6.85em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1006.85em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-588"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-589" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">0.13</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-590"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-591" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">λ</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-592"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-593"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-594" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">0</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-595" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">×</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-596" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">0.13</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-597"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.024em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-598" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">λ</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-599"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-600"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-601" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">0</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-69">0.13\lambda_{0}\times 0.13\lambda_{0}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The results of the simulated and measured input impedance are shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 7(a)</a>. The measured input impedance has a higher resonant frequency than the simulated one. Since the operating frequency of the antenna is sensitive to the parameters of the interdigital capacitor, as discussed in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec3" class="fulltext-link">Section III</a>, we believe that the disparity between the measured and simulated results is most likely caused by the fabrication error of the interdigital capacitors (especially the width <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-70-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-602" role="math" style="width: 3.727em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.366em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1003.31em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-603"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-604" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">w</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-605" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-606" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">0.3</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-70">w=0.3 </script></tex-math></inline-formula>mm and gap <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-71-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-607" role="math" style="width: 4.087em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.667em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1003.67em 2.586em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-608"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-609" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">g<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-610" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-611" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">0.24</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-71">g=0.24 </script></tex-math></inline-formula>mm in the interdigital capacitors since they are very close to the machining precision 0.2 mm). A larger width of loops can give more space for <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-72-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-612" role="math" style="width: 0.844em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.724em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.72em 2.345em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-613"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-614" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">w</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.67em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-72">w</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-73-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-615" role="math" style="width: 0.544em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.483em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1000.48em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-616"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-617" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">g<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-73">g</script></tex-math></inline-formula> so that the relative fabrication error can be reduced. The simulated and measured results for power reflection coefficient (PRC) <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref13" id="context_ref_13_4">[13]</a> are plotted in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 7(b)</a> for comparison. The operating frequency of the measured PRC is 925 MHz (while the operating frequency of the simulated PRC is 915 MHz), as the resonant frequency of the measured input impedance moves to higher frequency. The −3-dB bandwidth of PRC is 22 MHz in the simulated
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig8"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6478802/6590019/6590019-fig-8-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6478802/6590019/6590019-fig-8-small.gif" alt="Figure 8" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 8. </b><fig><p>Simulated radiation gain pattern of the proposed RFID tag antenna.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6590019/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig9"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6478802/6590019/6590019-fig-9-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6478802/6590019/6590019-fig-9-small.gif" alt="Figure 9" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 9. </b><fig><p>(a) Measured maximum reading range. (b) Reading range pattern in <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-74-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-618" role="math" style="width: 1.326em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.062em; height: 0px; font-size: 126%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.524em 1001.06em 2.583em -999.997em); top: -2.179em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-619"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-620" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">x</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-621" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">y<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.186em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.329em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.004em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-74">xy</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-plane of the proposed RFID tag antenna (unit: meters).</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6590019/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div> result and 23 MHz in the measured result. The simulated far-field radiation property is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8</a>. The gain deviation is less than 0.1 dB in the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-75-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-622" role="math" style="width: 1.204em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1001.08em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-623"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-624" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">x</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-625" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">y<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-75">xy</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-plane, which indicates a good omnidirectional radiation characteristic. With a simulated gain of −0.3 dB and a simulated radiation efficiency of 66%, the performance of the proposed antenna exceeds most other RFID antennas with similar sizes. The reading ranges are measured with an NI-VISN-100 RFID tester in a microwave anechoic chamber, from frequency 900 to 940 MHz. The total transmitted power is 4.0 W EIRP. The measured maximum reading range is 9.5 m at 925 MHz, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 9(a)</a>. The measured reading range pattern in the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-76-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-626" role="math" style="width: 1.204em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.565em 1001.08em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-627"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-628" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">x</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-629" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">y<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.87em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-76">xy</script></tex-math></inline-formula>-plane is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 9(b)</a>, and the range deviation is less than 0.2 m.<p></p><p>The reliability of the tag has been shown through simulation of the tag attached on host objects of different relative permittivities (1–10) with a distance of 2 mm. The radiation pattern of the tag is nearly unchanged, and the frequency deviation is within an acceptable range of less than 20 MHz.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec5"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION V.</div><h2>Conclusion</h2></div><p>In this letter, a capacitively loaded, inductively coupled fed loop RFID tag antenna with a horizontally omnidirectional radiation pattern has been proposed. The proposed antenna can be easily changed to other similar sizes and still achieve a good conjugate impedance matching condition. Compared to other tag antennas of similar size, it has a higher gain and a larger reading range and is less sensitive to the surrounding dielectric material. These advantages make it well suited for plate-tracking in catering businesses.</p></div>
</div></div>

<script>

function getCookie(name) {
	var nameEQ = name + "=";
	var ca = document.cookie.split(';');
	for(var i=0;i &lt; ca.length;i++) {
		var c = ca[i];
		while (c.charAt(0)==' ') c = c.substring(1,c.length);
		if (c.indexOf(nameEQ) == 0) return c.substring(nameEQ.length,c.length);
	}
	return null;
}

j$('document').ready(function(){
	if(getCookie('legacyUserName')!=null)
	{
		if(IBP_WS_ENABLED_FLAG){
		Modal.refreshLegacyAccountTransition('/xpl/mwLegacyAccountTransition.jsp');
		}
	}
});

</script>
